This controls the \\\"\\n125:                                            + \\\" durability of records that are sent. The following settings are allowed: \\\"\\n126:                                            + \\\" <ul>\\\"\\n127:                                            + \\\" <li><code>acks=0</code> If set to zero then the producer will not wait for any acknowledgment from the\\\"\\n128:                                            + \\\" server at all. The record will be immediately added to the socket buffer and considered sent. No guarantee can be\\\"\\n129:                                            + \\\" made that the server has received the record in this case, and the <code>retries</code> configuration will not\\\"\\n130:                                            + \\\" take effect (as the client won't generally know of any failures). The offset given back for each record will\\\"\\n131:                                            + \\\" always be set to <code>-1</code>.\\\"\\n132:                                            + \\\" <li><code>acks=1</code> This will mean the leader will write the record to its local log but will respond\\\"\\n133:                                            + \\\" without awaiting full acknowledgement from all followers. In this case should the leader fail immediately after\\\"\\n134:                                            + \\\" acknowledging the record but before the followers have replicated it then the record will be lost.\\\"\\n135:                                            + \\\" <li><code>acks=all</code> This means the leader will wait for the full set of in-sync replicas to\\\"\\n136:                                            + \\\" acknowledge the record. This guarantees that the record will not be lost as long as at least one in-sync replica\\\"\\n137:                                            + \\\" remains alive. This is the strongest available guarantee. This is equivalent to the acks=-1 setting.\\\"\\n138:                                            + \\\"</ul>\\\"\\n139:                                            + \\\"<p>\\\"\\n140:                                            + \\\"Note that enabling idempotence requires this config value to be 'all'.\\\"\\n141:                                            + \\\" If conflicting configurations are set and idempotence is not explicitly enabled, idempotence is disabled.\\\";\\n142: \\n143:     /** <code>linger.ms</code> */\\n144:     public static final String LINGER_MS_CONFIG = \\\"linger.ms\\\";\\n145:     private static final String LINGER_MS_DOC = \\\"The producer groups together any records that arrive in between request transmissions into a single batched request. \\\"\\n146:                                                 + \\\"Normally this occurs only under load when records arrive faster than they can be sent out. However in some circumstances the client may want to \\\"\\n147:                                                 + \\\"reduce the number of requests even under moderate load. This setting accomplishes this by adding a small amount \\\"\\n148:                                                 + \\\"of artificial delay&mdash;that is, rather than immediately sending out a record, the producer will wait for up to \\\"\\n149:                                                 + \\\"the given delay to allow other records to be sent so that the sends can be batched together. This can be thought \\\"\\n150:                                                 + \\\"of as analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. This setting gives the upper bound on the delay for batching: once \\\"\\n151:                                                 + \\\"we get <code>\\\" + BATCH_SIZE_CONFIG + \\\"</code> worth of records for a partition it will be sent immediately regardless of this \\\"\\n152:                                                 + \\\"setting, however if we have fewer than this many bytes accumulated for this partition we will 'linger' for the \\\"\\n153:                                                 + \\\"specified time waiting for more records to show up. Increasing <code>\\\" + LINGER_MS_CONFIG + \\\"=50</code>, \\\"\\n154:                                                 + \\\"for example, would have the effect of reducing the number of requests sent but would add up to 50ms of latency to records sent in the absence of load.\\\"\\n155:                                                 + \\\"The default changed from 0 to 5 in Apache Kafka 4.0 as the efficiency gains from larger batches typically result in \\\"\\n156:                                                 + \\\"similar or lower producer latency despite the increased linger.\\\";\\n157: \\n158:     /** <code>request.timeout.ms</code> */\\n159:     public static final String REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG = CommonClientConfigs.REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG;\\n160:     private static final String REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC = CommonClientConfigs.REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC\\n161:         + \\\" This should be larger than <code>replica.lag.time.max.ms</code> (a broker configuration)\\\"\\n162:         + \\\" to reduce the possibility of message duplication due to unnecessary producer retries.\\\";\\n163: \\n164:     /** <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> */\\n165:     public static final String DELIVERY_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG = \\\"delivery.timeout.ms\\\";\\n166:     private static final String DELIVERY_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC = \\\"An upper bound on the time to report success or failure \\\"\\n167:             + \\\"after a call to <code>send()</code> returns. \\\"acks\\\";\\n124:     private static final String ACKS_DOC = \\\"The number of acknowledgments the producer requires the leader to have received before considering a request complete. This controls the \\\"\\n125:                                            + \\\" durability of records that are sent. The following settings are allowed: \\\"\\n126:                                            + \\\" <ul>\\\"\\n127:                                            + \\\" <li><code>acks=0</code> If set to zero then the producer will not wait for any acknowledgment from the\\\"\\n128:                                            + \\\" server at all. The record will be immediately added to the socket buffer and considered sent. No guarantee can be\\\"\\n129:                                            + \\\" made that the server has received the record in this case, and the <code>retries</code> configuration will not\\\"\\n130:                                            + \\\" take effect (as the client won't generally know of any failures). The offset given back for each record will\\\"\\n131:                                            + \\\" always be set to <code>-1</code>.\\\"\\n132:                                            + \\\" <li><code>acks=1</code> This will mean the leader will write the record to its local log but will respond\\\"\\n133:                                            + \\\" without awaiting full acknowledgement from all followers. In this case should the leader fail immediately after\\\"\\n134:                                            + \\\" acknowledging the record but before the followers have replicated it then the record will be lost.\\\"\\n135:                                            + \\\" <li><code>acks=all</code> This means the leader will wait for the full set of in-sync replicas to\\\"\\n136:                                            + \\\" acknowledge the record. This guarantees that the record will not be lost as long as at least one in-sync replica\\\"\\n137:                                            + \\\" remains alive. This is the strongest available guarantee. This is equivalent to the acks=-1 setting.\\\"\\n138:                                            + \\\"</ul>\\\"\\n139:                                            + \\\"<p>\\\"\\n140:                                            + \\\"Note that enabling idempotence requires this config value to be 'all'.\\\"\\n141:                                            + \\\" If conflicting configurations are set and idempotence is not explicitly enabled, idempotence is disabled.\\\";\\n142: \\n143:     /** <code>linger.ms</code> */\\n144:     public static final String LINGER_MS_CONFIG = \\\"linger.ms\\\";\\n145:     private static final String LINGER_MS_DOC = \\\"The producer groups together any records that arrive in between request transmissions into a single batched request. \\\"\\n146:                                                 + \\\"Normally this occurs only under load when records arrive faster than they can be sent out. However in some circumstances the client may want to \\\"\\n147:                                                 + \\\"reduce the number of requests even under moderate load. This setting accomplishes this by adding a small amount \\\"\\n148:                                                 + \\\"of artificial delay&mdash;that is, rather than immediately sending out a record, the producer will wait for up to \\\"\\n149:                                                 + \\\"the given delay to allow other records to be sent so that the sends can be batched together. This can be thought \\\"\\n150:                                                 + \\\"of as analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. This setting gives the upper bound on the delay for batching: once \\\"\\n151:                                                 + \\\"we get <code>\\\" + BATCH_SIZE_CONFIG + \\\"</code> worth of records for a partition it will be sent immediately regardless of this \\\"\\n152:                                                 + \\\"setting, however if we have fewer than this many bytes accumulated for this partition we will 'linger' for the \\\"\\n153:                                                 + \\\"specified time waiting for more records to show up. This setting defaults to 5 (i.e. 5ms delay). Increasing <code>\\\" + LINGER_MS_CONFIG + \\\"=50</code>, \\\"\\n154:                                                 + \\\"for example, would have the effect of reducing the number of requests sent but would add up to 50ms of latency to records sent in the absence of load.\\\"\\n155:                                                 + \\\"The default changed from 0 to 5 in Apache Kafka 4.0 as the efficiency gains from larger batches typically result in \\\"\\n156:                                                 + \\\"similar or lower producer latency despite the increased linger.\\\";\\n157: \\n158:     /** <code>request.timeout.ms</code> */\\n159:     public static final String REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG = CommonClientConfigs.REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG;\\n160:     private static final String REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC = CommonClientConfigs.REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC\\n161:         + \\\" This should be larger than <code>replica.lag.time.max.ms</code> (a broker configuration)\\\"\\n162:         + \\\" to reduce the possibility of message duplication due to unnecessary producer retries.\\\";\\n163: \\n164:     /** <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> */\\n165:     public static final String DELIVERY_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG = \\\"delivery.timeout.ms\\\";\\n166:     private static final String DELIVERY_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC = \\\"An upper bound on the time to report success or failure \\\"\\n167:             + \\\"after a call to <code>send()</code> returns. No guarantee can be\"\n129:                                            + \" made that the server has received the record in this case, and the <code>retries</code> configuration will not\"\n130:                                            + \" take effect (as the client won't generally know of any failures). The offset given back for each record will\"\n131:                                            + \" always be set to <code>-1</code>.\"\n132:                                            + \" <li><code>acks=1</code> This will mean the leader will write the record to its local log but will respond\"\n133:                                            + \" without awaiting full acknowledgement from all followers. In this case should the leader fail immediately after\"\n134:                                            + \" acknowledging the record but before the followers have replicated it then the record will be lost.\"\n135:                                            + \" <li><code>acks=all</code> This means the leader will wait for the full set of in-sync replicas to\"\n136:                                            + \" acknowledge the record. This guarantees that the record will not be lost as long as at least one in-sync replica\"\n137:                                            + \" remains alive. This is the strongest available guarantee. This is equivalent to the acks=-1 setting.\"\n138:                                            + \"</ul>\"\n139:                                            + \"<p>\"\n140:                                            + \"Note that enabling idempotence requires this config value to be 'all'.\"\n141:                                            + \" If conflicting configurations are set and idempotence is not explicitly enabled, idempotence is disabled.\";\n142: \n143:     /** <code>linger.ms</code> */\n144:     public static final String LINGER_MS_CONFIG = \"linger.ms\";\n145:     private static final String LINGER_MS_DOC = \"The producer groups together any records that arrive in between request transmissions into a single batched request. \"\n146:                                                 + \"Normally this occurs only under load when records arrive faster than they can be sent out. However in some circumstances the client may want to \"\n147:                                                 + \"reduce the number of requests even under moderate load. This setting accomplishes this by adding a small amount \"\n148:                                                 + \"of artificial delay&mdash;that is, rather than immediately sending out a record, the producer will wait for up to \"\n149:                                                 + \"the given delay to allow other records to be sent so that the sends can be batched together. This can be thought \"\n150:                                                 + \"of as analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. This setting gives the upper bound on the delay for batching: once \"\n151:                                                 + \"we get <code>\" + BATCH_SIZE_CONFIG + \"</code> worth of records for a partition it will be sent immediately regardless of this \"\n152:                                                 + \"setting, however if we have fewer than this many bytes accumulated for this partition we will 'linger' for the \"\n153:                                                 + \"specified time waiting for more records to show up. This setting defaults to 5 (i.e. 5ms delay). Increasing <code>\" + LINGER_MS_CONFIG + \"=50</code>, \"\n154:                                                 + \"for example, would have the effect of reducing the number of requests sent but would add up to 50ms of latency to records sent in the absence of load.\"\n155:                                                 + \"The default changed from 0 to 5 in Apache Kafka 4.0 as the efficiency gains from larger batches typically result in \"\n156:                                                 + \"similar or lower producer latency despite the increased linger.\";\n157: \n158:     /** <code>request.timeout.ms</code> */\n159:     public static final String REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG = CommonClientConfigs.REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG;\n160:     private static final String REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC = CommonClientConfigs.REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC\n161:         + \" This should be larger than <code>replica.lag.time.max.ms</code> (a broker configuration)\"\n162:         + \" to reduce the possibility of message duplication due to unnecessary producer retries.\";\n163: \n164:     /** <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> */\n165:     public static final String DELIVERY_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG = \"delivery.timeout.ms\";\n166:     private static final String DELIVERY_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC = \"An upper bound on the time to report success or failure \"\n167:             + \"after a call to <code>send()</code> returns.
